"THE

CACHUCHA."

i

2 7 , 1837.

" M r s . Stirling's performance of Pascal Bruno was most admirable;
a better representation could not have been given of an Italian Bandit.
Mr. W r i g h t ' s Captain Altaville was second only to some of Mr. J . Reeve's
performances in his best days."
Morning
Herald.
" M r . W r i g h t acted with a good deal of quiet humour, and danced
in the closing scene with an extravagance which elicited hearty peals of
laughter."
TMorning Chronicle,
"Pascal Bruno, the hero of last night, was well sustained by Mrs.
Stirling, who lost none of her fascination by the assumption of the rude and
masculine attire of the Palermo Peasant, with the advantageous aid of a pair
of formidable wThiskers, and a smart imperial on the tip of one of the
prettiest chins in the .world, she seemed much more likely to do mischief
amongst the unsophisticated maidens of Sicily, than the fierce hero whom she
represented. W e confess that we have seldom seen this interesting actress
-to greater advantage than in t h e character of this dashing and daringBrigand, whom the genius of Alexandre Dumas, united to the taste of th*enterprising Manager, last night presented t > a fashionable and discriminating audience. T h e piece was quite successful. The Scenery was of a
character t o maintain the reputation which this house hitherto has held for
tasteful decoration; the Scenes particularly deserving of notice, a r e a
Mountainous Pass in Sieily, a splendid Apartment in the Viceroy's Villa, and
a Saloon in the Palace of Prince Butera, in which a Masqued Ball takes
place on a scale of unrivalled magnificence * the Fortress of Pascal Bruno,
was also represented with much pictorial power."
Morning
Advertiser.
i(

At the conclusion of the Burletta, the public displayed their zeal in the
loud calls for the appearance of Mrs. Stirling."
Times.

"Pascal Bruno, the hero of last night, was well sustained by Mrs.
Stirling, who lost none of her fascination by the assumption of the rude and
masculine attire of the Palermo Peasant, with the advantageous aid of a pair
of formidable whiske.s, and a smart imperial on the tip of one of the
prettiest chins i i r t l i e world, she seemed much more likely to do mischief
among*st the unsophisticated maidens of .Sicily, than the fierce hei*o whom she
represented. W e confess that we have seldom seen this interesting actress
to greater a«.'vantage than in t h e ehatacter of this dashing and daring
Brigand, whom the genius of Alexandre Dumas, united to the taste of the
enterprising Manager, last Dight presented t» a fashionable and discriminating audience. T h e piece was quite successful. T h e Scenery was of a
character to maintain the reputation which this house hitherto has held for
tasteful decoration; the Scenes particularly deserving of notice, a r e a
Mountainous P,iss in Sicily, a splendid Apartment in the Viceroy's Villa, and
a Saloon in the Palace of Prince Butera, in which a Masqued Ball takes
place on a scale of unrivalled magnificence J the Fortress of Pascal Bruno,
was also represented with much pictorial power.*'
Morning
Advertiser.

"Mrs. Stirling's performance of Pa*cal Bruno was most admirable;
a better representation could not have been given of an Italian Bandit.
Mr. W r i g h t ' s Captain Altaville was second only t o some of Mr. J . Reeve's
performances in his best days."
Morning
Herald.
" M r . Wright acted with a good deal of quiet humour, and danced
in the closing scene with an extravagance which elicited hearty peals of
laughter."
Morning' Chronicle.
"Pascal Bruno, the hero of last night, was well sustained by Mrs.
Stirling, who lost none of her fascination by the assumption of the rude and
masculine attire of the Palermo Peasant, with the advantageous aid of a pair
of formidable whiskers, and a imart imperial on the tip of one of the
prettiest chins in the world, she seemed much mote likely to do mischief
amongst the unsophisticated maidens of Sicily, than the fierce hero whom she
represented. W e confess that we have seldom seen this interesting actress
to greater advantage than in t h e character of this dashing and daring
Brigand, whom the genius of Alexandre Dumas, united to the taste of the
enterprising Manager, last night presented t.» a fashionable and discriminating audience. T h e piece was quite successful. The Scenery was of a
character to maintain the reputation which this house hitherto has held for
tasteful decoration; the Scenes particularly deserving of notice, are a
Mountainous Pass in Sicily, a splendid Apartment in the Viceroy's Villa, and
a Saioon in the Palace of Prince Butera, in which a Masqued Ball takes
place on a scale of unrivalled magnificence; the Fortress of Pascal Bruno,
was also represented with much pictorial power."
Morning
Advertiser.
